OCTOBER TERM, 1999

\n

Decree

\n

UNITED STATES v. ALASKA

\n

on bill of complaint

\n

No. 84, Orig. Decided June 19, 1997\xe2\x80\x94Decree entered June 29, 2000

\n

Decree entered.

\n

Opinion reported: 521 U. S. 1.

\n

The joint motion for entry of a decree is granted.

\n

DECREE

\n

On June 18, 1979, the Court granted the United States\nleave to file a bill of complaint setting out a dispute over the\nrights of the United States and the State of Alaska to offer\nlands in the Beaufort Sea for mineral leasing. 442 U. S. 937.\nThe Court appointed a Special Master to direct subsequent\nproceedings and to submit such reports as he deemed appropriate. 444 U. S. 1065 (1980). The Court later referred\nto the Master the State of Alaska\'s motion for leave to file\na counterclaim seeking a decree quieting its title to coastal\nsubmerged lands within two federal reservations, the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska and the Arctic National\nWildlife Range (now known as the Arctic National Wildlife\nRefuge). 445 U. S. 914 (1980).

\n

From 1980 through 1986, the Master oversaw extensive\nhearings and briefing. On May 20, 1996, the Court received\nand ordered filed the Special Master\'s Report. 517 U. S.\n1207. On June 19, 1997, this Court overruled Alaska\'s exceptions, sustained the United States\' exception, and directed the parties to prepare and submit an appropriate\ndecree, consistent with the Court\'s decision, for the Court\'s\nconsideration. 521 U. S. 1. The parties have prepared a\nproposed decree and have recommended its entry by the\nCourt.

\n

Accordingly,

\n

1021

\n
\n

UNITED STATES v. ALASKA

\n

Decree

\n

IT IS ORDERED, ADJUDGED, AND DECREED:

\n

A. Alaska\'s Motion for Leave to File a Counterclaim.

\n

The motion of the State of Alaska for leave to file a counterclaim is granted.

\n

B. The Federal-State Boundary Marking the Seaward Extent of the State of Alaska\'s Submerged Lands Act Grant.

\n

1. Except as provided in Paragraph C below, as against\nthe State of Alaska and all persons claiming under it, the\nUnited States has exclusive rights to explore the area lying\nseaward of the line described in Exhibit A hereof and to\nexploit the natural resources of said area. The State of\nAlaska is not entitled to any interest in such lands, minerals,\nand resources, except as may be provided by \xc2\xa7 8(g) of the\nOuter Continental Shelf Lands Act, 67 Stat. 468, 43 U. S. C.\n\xc2\xa7 1337(g), and Paragraph C of this Decree. The State of\nAlaska, its privies, assigns, lessees, and other persons claiming under it are hereby enjoined from interfering with the\nrights of the United States in such lands, minerals, and\nresources.

\n

2. Except as provided in Paragraph C below and except\nwithin the boundaries of the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska and the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge, and subject to the exceptions set out in \xc2\xa7 5 of the Submerged Lands\nAct, 67 Stat. 32, 43 U. S. C. \xc2\xa7 1313, as against the United\nStates and all persons claiming under it, the State of Alaska\nhas exclusive rights to explore the area lying shoreward of\nthe line described in Exhibit A hereof and to exploit the natural resources of said area. The United States is not entitled to any interest in such lands, minerals, and resources\nexcept as may be provided by Paragraph C of this Decree.\nThe United States, its privies, assigns, lessees, and other\npersons claiming under it are hereby enjoined from interfering with the rights of the State of Alaska in such lands, minerals, and resources.

\n

1022

\n
\n

Cite as: 530 U. S. 1021 (2000)

\n

Decree

\n

3. The boundary described in Exhibit A shall remain fixed\nfor purposes of the Submerged Lands Act.

\n

C. Distribution of Revenues in Escrow and Administration of Leases.

\n

1. The United States and the State of Alaska shall resolve\naccounting and administration issues arising from the past\nissuance of offshore oil and gas leases in disputed areas based\non the following principles:

\n

a. Existing and Former Leases That Are Subject to\n\xc2\xa7 7 Agreements. During the course of this litigation,\nthe United States and the State of Alaska entered into\nagreements under \xc2\xa7 7 of the Outer Continental Shelf\nLands Act, 43 U. S. C. \xc2\xa7 1336, and Alaska Stat.\n\xc2\xa7\xc2\xa7 38.05.020 and 38.05.137, to allow mineral leasing of\nsubmerged lands in disputed areas. Under the terms\nof those "\xc2\xa7 7 Agreements," lease revenues are held in\nincome-producing escrow accounts for distribution based\non the outcome of the litigation. No later than 180 days\nafter entry of this Decree, the funds held in escrow accounts shall be distributed in accordance with the distribution provisions contained in the \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements. The\nUnited States and the State of Alaska shall carry out all\napplicable provisions and terms of the \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements\nand shall administer the leases in accordance with the\nprovisions therein. \nb. Existing and Former Leases That Are Affected by\nthe Fixed Federal-State Boundary Described in Exhibit \nA. The United States and the State of Alaska have issued mineral leases in offshore areas that were not in\ndispute on the date of lease issuance and are therefore\nnot subject to \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements. Those leases may be intersected, however, by the fixed federal-state boundary\ndescribed in Exhibit A, which is based upon surveys conducted after the lease dates. Leases existing on the

The joint motion for entry of a decree is granted.

\n

DECREE

\n

On June 18, 1979, the Court granted the United States\nleave to file a bill of complaint setting out a dispute over the\nrights of the United States and the State of Alaska to offer\nlands in the Beaufort Sea for mineral leasing. 442 U. S. 937.\nThe Court appointed a Special Master to direct subsequent\nproceedings and to submit such reports as he deemed appropriate. 444 U. S. 1065 (1980). The Court later referred\nto the Master the State of Alaska\'s motion for leave to file\na counterclaim seeking a decree quieting its title to coastal\nsubmerged lands within two federal reservations, the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska and the Arctic National\nWildlife Range (now known as the Arctic National Wildlife\nRefuge). 445 U. S. 914 (1980).

\n

From 1980 through 1986, the Master oversaw extensive\nhearings and briefing. On May 20, 1996, the Court received\nand ordered filed the Special Master\'s Report. 517 U. S.\n1207. On June 19, 1997, this Court overruled Alaska\'s exceptions, sustained the United States\' exception, and directed the parties to prepare and submit an appropriate\ndecree, consistent with the Court\'s decision, for the Court\'s\nconsideration. 521 U. S. 1. The parties have prepared a\nproposed decree and have recommended its entry by the\nCourt.

\n

Accordingly,

\n

\n
\n

UNITED STATES v. ALASKA

\n

Decree

\n

IT IS ORDERED, ADJUDGED, AND DECREED:

\n

A. Alaska\'s Motion for Leave to File a Counterclaim.

\n

The motion of the State of Alaska for leave to file a counterclaim is granted.

\n

B. The Federal-State Boundary Marking the Seaward Extent of the State of Alaska\'s Submerged Lands Act Grant.

\n

1. Except as provided in Paragraph C below, as against\nthe State of Alaska and all persons claiming under it, the\nUnited States has exclusive rights to explore the area lying\nseaward of the line described in Exhibit A hereof and to\nexploit the natural resources of said area. The State of\nAlaska is not entitled to any interest in such lands, minerals,\nand resources, except as may be provided by \xc2\xa7 8(g) of the\nOuter Continental Shelf Lands Act, 67 Stat. 468, 43 U. S. C.\n\xc2\xa7 1337(g), and Paragraph C of this Decree. The State of\nAlaska, its privies, assigns, lessees, and other persons claiming under it are hereby enjoined from interfering with the\nrights of the United States in such lands, minerals, and\nresources.

\n

2. Except as provided in Paragraph C below and except\nwithin the boundaries of the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska and the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge, and subject to the exceptions set out in \xc2\xa7 5 of the Submerged Lands\nAct, 67 Stat. 32, 43 U. S. C. \xc2\xa7 1313, as against the United\nStates and all persons claiming under it, the State of Alaska\nhas exclusive rights to explore the area lying shoreward of\nthe line described in Exhibit A hereof and to exploit the natural resources of said area. The United States is not entitled to any interest in such lands, minerals, and resources\nexcept as may be provided by Paragraph C of this Decree.\nThe United States, its privies, assigns, lessees, and other\npersons claiming under it are hereby enjoined from interfering with the rights of the State of Alaska in such lands, minerals, and resources.

\n

1022

\n
\n

Cite as: 530 U. S. 1021 (2000)

\n

Decree

\n

3. The boundary described in Exhibit A shall remain fixed\nfor purposes of the Submerged Lands Act.

\n

C. Distribution of Revenues in Escrow and Administration of Leases.

\n

1. The United States and the State of Alaska shall resolve\naccounting and administration issues arising from the past\nissuance of offshore oil and gas leases in disputed areas based\non the following principles:

\n

a. Existing and Former Leases That Are Subject to\n\xc2\xa7 7 Agreements. During the course of this litigation,\nthe United States and the State of Alaska entered into\nagreements under \xc2\xa7 7 of the Outer Continental Shelf\nLands Act, 43 U. S. C. \xc2\xa7 1336, and Alaska Stat.\n\xc2\xa7\xc2\xa7 38.05.020 and 38.05.137, to allow mineral leasing of\nsubmerged lands in disputed areas. Under the terms\nof those "\xc2\xa7 7 Agreements," lease revenues are held in\nincome-producing escrow accounts for distribution based\non the outcome of the litigation. No later than 180 days\nafter entry of this Decree, the funds held in escrow accounts shall be distributed in accordance with the distribution provisions contained in the \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements. The\nUnited States and the State of Alaska shall carry out all\napplicable provisions and terms of the \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements\nand shall administer the leases in accordance with the\nprovisions therein. \nb. Existing and Former Leases That Are Affected by\nthe Fixed Federal-State Boundary Described in Exhibit \nA. The United States and the State of Alaska have issued mineral leases in offshore areas that were not in\ndispute on the date of lease issuance and are therefore\nnot subject to \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements. Those leases may be intersected, however, by the fixed federal-state boundary\ndescribed in Exhibit A, which is based upon surveys conducted after the lease dates. Leases existing on the

\n

1023

\n
\n

UNITED STATES v. ALASKA

\n

Decree

\n

date of this Decree and not covered by \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements,\nbut intersected by the fixed federal-state boundary described in Exhibit A, shall continue to be administered\nby the original lessor, who shall have the exclusive right\nto all past and future revenues from the lease. Following the expiration, relinquishment, or termination of\nsuch leases, the rights to explore and exploit the natural\nresources within the area that was leased shall be determined solely in accordance with Paragraph B of this Decree. The distribution of revenues from former leases\nthat expired before the date of this Decree, that were\nnot covered by \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements, but that would have\nbeen intersected by the fixed federal-state boundary described in Exhibit A, shall not be affected by the fixing\nof the federal-state boundary. \nc. Existing and Former Leases That Are Both Subject to \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements and A ffected by the Fixed\nFederal-State Boundary Described in Exhibit A. In\nthe event that an existing lease is subject to a \xc2\xa7 7 Agreement and is intersected by the fixed federal-state boundary described in Exhibit A, the funds held in escrow\nshall be distributed, and the lease shall be administered,\nin accordance with the provisions of the \xc2\xa7 7 Agreement.\nFollowing the expiration, relinquishment, or termination\nof the lease, the rights to explore and exploit the natural\nresources within the area that was leased shall be determined solely in accordance with Paragraph B of this Decree. The distribution of revenues from former leases\nthat expired before the date of this Decree, that were\nsubject to \xc2\xa7 7 Agreements, but that would have been intersected by the fixed federal-state boundary described\nin Exhibit A, shall not be affected by the fixing of the\nfederal-state boundary.

\n

2. This Decree shall not affect the rights or obligations\nof the United States or the State of Alaska with respect to

\n

1024

\n
\n

Cite as: 530 U. S. 1021 (2000)

\n

Decree

\n

its lessees or third parties, whether arising from the \xc2\xa7 7\nAgreements or otherwise. This Decree shall not affect any\nrights or obligations arising under present or future unitization, operating, enhanced recovery, commingling, or other\nsimilar agreements between the parties or with others.

\n

D. The Coastal Boundary of the National Petroleum\nReserve-Alaska.

\n

The coastal boundary of the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska is a continuous line, as described in Executive Order\nNo. 3739-A (1923), in Presidential Executive Orders (1980)\n(microform, reel 6), that begins at the western bank of the\nColville River and follows the highest highwater mark west-erly, extending across the entrances of small lagoons, including Peard Bay, Wainwright Inlet, the Kuk River, Kugrua\nBay and River, and other small bays and river estuaries,\nand following the ocean side of barrier islands and sandspits\nwithin three miles of shore and the ocean side of the Plover\nIslands, to the northwestern extremity of Icy Cape, approximately 70\xc2\xb0 21[H11541] N., 161\xc2\xb0 46[H11541] W.

\n

E. The Coastal Boundary of the Arctic National Wildlife\nRefuge.

\n

The coastal boundary of the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge is a continuous line, as described in Public Land Order\nNo. 2214, 25 Fed. Reg. 12598 (1960), that begins at the intersection of the International Boundary line between the State\nof Alaska and Yukon Territory, Canada, with the line of extreme low water of the Arctic Ocean in the vicinity of Monument 1 of said International Boundary line, and follows the\nline of extreme low water westerly, extending across the entrances of lagoons such that all offshore bars, reefs and islands, and lagoons that separate them from the mainland,\nare part of the Refuge, to Brownlow Point, at approximately\n70\xc2\xb0 10[H11541] N., 145\xc2\xb0 51[H11541] W.

\n

1025

\n
\n

UNITED STATES v. ALASKA

\n

Decree

\n

F. Resolution of Disputes Respecting the Coastal Boundaries of the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska and the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge.

\n

The coastal boundaries of the National Petroleum Reserve-Alaska and the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge are ambulatory and will therefore migrate as a result of changes in relevant physical features. The United States and the State\nof Alaska may resolve disputes arising from those changes\nthrough negotiation, through alternative methods of dispute\nresolution, or through invocation of this Court\'s retained\njurisdiction in accordance with Paragraph G. The United\nStates and the State of Alaska may jointly submit to this\nCourt, for entry as a supplement to this Decree, any agreement respecting the location of the coastal boundary of the\nNational Petroleum Reserve-Alaska or of the Arctic National Wildlife Refuge.

\n

G. Retention of Jurisdiction.

\n

The Court retains jurisdiction to entertain such further\nproceedings, enter such orders, and issue such writs as from\ntime to time may be determined necessary or advisable to\neffectuate and supplement this Decree and the rights of the\nrespective parties. In all other respects, this Decree is final.

\n

The line is fixed\nby coordinates based on the North American Datum 1983\n(NAD 83), which is equivalent to the World Geodetic System 1984 (WGS 84). For convenience, the coordinates are\nalso set out by reference to the North American Datum\n1927 (NAD 27). The NAD 83 coordinates are authoritative for purposes of this Decree.
